  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_67ba2e99-49db-43fa-a001-e58f8d633a91'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14267797936650342085">The year is 340 BC. A hunted, haunted Brahmin youth vows revenge for the gruesome murder of his beloved father. Cold, calculating, cruel and armed with a complete absence of accepted morals, he becomes the most powerful political strategist in Bharat and succeeds in uniting a ragged country against the invasion of the army of that demigod, Alexander the Great. Pitting the </span>
  <span id="freeText14267797936650342085" style="display:none">The year is 340 BC. A hunted, haunted Brahmin youth vows revenge for the gruesome murder of his beloved father. Cold, calculating, cruel and armed with a complete absence of accepted morals, he becomes the most powerful political strategist in Bharat and succeeds in uniting a ragged country against the invasion of the army of that demigod, Alexander the Great. Pitting the weak edges of both forces against each other, he pulls off a wicked and astonishing victory and succeeds in installing Chandragupta on the throne of the mighty Mauryan empire.<br /><br />History knows him as the brilliant strategist Chanakya. Satisfied—and a little bored—by his success as a kingmaker, through the simple summoning of his gifted mind, he recedes into the shadows to write his Arthashastra, the ‘science of wealth’. But history, which exults in repeating itself, revives Chanakya two and a half millennia later, in the avatar of Gangasagar Mishra, a Brahmin teacher in smalltown India who becomes puppeteer to a host of ambitious individuals—including a certain slumchild who grows up into a beautiful and powerful woman.<br /><br />Modern India happens to be just as riven as ancient Bharat by class hatred, corruption and divisive politics and this landscape is Gangasagar’s feasting ground. Can this wily pandit—who preys on greed, venality and sexual deviance—bring about another miracle of a united India? Will Chanakya’s chant work again? Ashwin Sanghi, the bestselling author of The Rozabal Line, brings you yet another historical spinechiller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14267797936650342085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/177599-why-did-gangasagar-want-chandini-to-be-the">Why did Gangasagar want Chandini to be the Prime Minister. Chanakya&#39;s motive was to avenge his father&#39;s death and put an end to Dhananda&#39;s rule... but what about Gangasagar?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_177599'><a id="like_count_community_question_177599" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/177599?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F10098912-chanakya-s-chant">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/177599-why-did-gangasagar-want-chandini-to-be-the">6 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/177599-why-did-gangasagar-want-chandini-to-be-the">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37700050-vaibhav-vats"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1417974571i/37700050._UX100_CR0,28,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37700050-vaibhav-vats">Vaibhav Vats</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Chanakya's motive to avenge his father's death is one thing. Chankya picked Chandragupta Maurya(a child) to be the emperor of Magadh is another thing <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Chanakya's motive to avenge his father's death is one thing. Chankya picked Chandragupta Maurya(a child) to be the emperor of Magadh is another thing based on his abilities as a young child. Similarly Gangasagar picked Chandini to be PM was based on her childhood abilities (the way she used to answer his classroom questions). Gangasagar had nothing to avenge for, he was just after power; intellectual powers and political powers. And Chanakya was after revenge and shape a better future for India. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1268799-chandini-is-in-3rd-term-as-pm-harry-age">Chandini is in 3rd term as PM. Harry age in 21 at the end of the book. She gave birth at collage, so lets keep her age as 20 at that time. The different between their age is 20, if Harry is 21 she must be 41. But according to rule &quot;To become PM one must be atleast 35 years old&quot;. According to book if is serving 3rd time how did she beacame PM in the age of atleas 30?</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/28044134-mani-sankar"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/28044134-mani-sankar">Mani Sankar</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
There is no minimum age to become PM. Any MP can become a PM. So if the MP is from Loksabha then minimum age is 25 and 30 for Rajyasabha.
</span>
</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_283682588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283682588" />
    <a title="Prashanth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7779662-prashanth"><img alt="Prashanth" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283682588?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Prashanth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Prashanth" href="/user/show/7779662-prashanth">Prashanth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283682588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8051041352754310217">Grievously disappointing- neither story feels authentic; the character development is shallow, the conversation inane, the victories too easily attained. There is also no effort to match the conversational idiom with the historical context in which the stories are supposedly set, the time lines of both the story-strands are obfuscated due to the lack of attention to details and the inconsistencies (A few examples: "Ashoka trees" are referred to in the Maurya tale for e.g., while Ashoka was Chand</span>
  <span id="freeText8051041352754310217" style="display:none">Grievously disappointing- neither story feels authentic; the character development is shallow, the conversation inane, the victories too easily attained. There is also no effort to match the conversational idiom with the historical context in which the stories are supposedly set, the time lines of both the story-strands are obfuscated due to the lack of attention to details and the inconsistencies (A few examples: "Ashoka trees" are referred to in the Maurya tale for e.g., while Ashoka was Chandragupta's grandson, there is a reference to "Afghanistan" as well predating the first mention of that name by at least 2000 years, UP is supposed to send 85 MPs and Bihar 54- these are pre-2000 figures before the formation of Uttarakhand and Jharkhand respectively- but the other references to current events such as cash-for-votes, etc are very contemporary, to just name a few off-the-cuff, there are a myriad others). The dialogues are so uninspired as to be excruciating- they borrow liberally and unimaginatively from a random book of quotations and also the delectable BBC TV series "Yes Minister" and "Yes Prime Minister" for effect, and are served up simplistically without any respect whatsoever for the reader's intelligence. <br /><br />One wonders why the author could not have taken the effort to make the dialogues more original and effective by recasting whatever pearls of wisdom he found relevant to his tales in his own words, and in a much wittier manner.To the author's credit, he does provide a list of references and acknowledgments for his research in which the reader's suspicions are confirmed- that this novel was intellectually and in literary terms an effort steeped in complacence and mediocrity,(if not outright indolence) and by relying on regurgitation of popular quotes for inspiration fritters away magnificently, a great opportunity to not only revitalize, by retelling, an ancient Indian tale but also to comment with insight and wisdom on the murky world of contemporary Indian politics. Will be meticulously laying off Ashwin Sanghi's works in future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8051041352754310217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_761175237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761175237" />
    <a title="Amrita Chatwal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12829953-amrita-chatwal"><img alt="Amrita Chatwal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347642052p2/12829953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761175237?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amrita Chatwal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amrita Chatwal" href="/user/show/12829953-amrita-chatwal">Amrita Chatwal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761175237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4945979177505319886">What IS it with Indian writers? Why does it take time and a substantial number of pages before you can get used to their style of writing? I had the same problem with Amish Tripathi and now with Sanghi.<br/><br/>I started this book with the hope of learning something about India in the 4th century. I finished this book only because the neatnik in me refuses to leave a book half-read. <br/><br/>Two parallel narratives - one centered around Chanakya's machinations, the other around Chanakya's modern avatar, Gangasaga</span>
  <span id="freeText4945979177505319886" style="display:none">What IS it with Indian writers? Why does it take time and a substantial number of pages before you can get used to their style of writing? I had the same problem with Amish Tripathi and now with Sanghi.<br /><br />I started this book with the hope of learning something about India in the 4th century. I finished this book only because the neatnik in me refuses to leave a book half-read. <br /><br />Two parallel narratives - one centered around Chanakya's machinations, the other around Chanakya's modern avatar, Gangasagar Mishra - are the only thing that prevent this book from plunging into unadulterated, teeth-gritting boredom. Just when you feel that you'd like to strangle Chanakya for being an inhuman, overthinking clod, along comes Gangasagar to remind you that the dregs of the world of fictional characters are vastly populated indeed. <br /><br />The subject and storyline of the book could have been fairly interesting if they hadn't been bogged down by the soulless writing and flat characters. Even with two narratives, the book is hopelessly one-dimensional. The writing is more like reporting, except when Sanghi remembers that it's supposed to be creative fiction and inserts a sentence or two to appease the more discerning. <br /><br />What irked me most about the book, perhaps irrationally, was the liberal use of quotes from personalities as varied as Dale Carnegie and Joseph Stalin. It was downright incongruous to read about a 4th century Brahmin quoting Mae West. It was an exercise in self-control to stop my eyes rolling in frustration whenever Chanakya or Gangasagar glibly spouted yet another quote. <br /><br />The book is being relegated to the back of my book shelf. If only to hide from myself the reminder that I'm hopelessly inable to prevent the automatic movement of my eyeballs and eyebrows when confronted with bullshit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4945979177505319886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_424894709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/424894709" />
    <a title="Samadrita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13266158-samadrita"><img alt="Samadrita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461258628p2/13266158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/424894709?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samadrita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samadrita" href="/user/show/13266158-samadrita">Samadrita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=suspense-thrillers">suspense-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=sort-of-good">sort-of-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=human-drama">human-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=india">india</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=crime-noir">crime-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=bygones-are-never-bygones">bygones-are-never-bygones</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer424894709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6338608994737827961"><i>Chanakya's Chant</i> is not one but two similarly-themed novels, spanning across two different timelines, combined into one thrilling roller-coaster ride that you are bound to enjoy throughout.<br/><br/><i>The first story follows the machinations of the ingenious Brahmin Chanakya, who mentors a young Chandragupta Maurya, right from childhood into finally ascending the throne of Magadh, the most powerful kingdom in ancient India. The latter one deals with Gangasagar Mishra, a Chanakya-like character, who plays ki</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6338608994737827961" style="display:none"><i>Chanakya's Chant</i> is not one but two similarly-themed novels, spanning across two different timelines, combined into one thrilling roller-coaster ride that you are bound to enjoy throughout.<br /><br /><i>The first story follows the machinations of the ingenious Brahmin Chanakya, who mentors a young Chandragupta Maurya, right from childhood into finally ascending the throne of Magadh, the most powerful kingdom in ancient India. The latter one deals with Gangasagar Mishra, a Chanakya-like character, who plays kingmaker in modern India.<br />The book begins on an eerie note as we are introduced to an ailing Gangasagar Mishra, awaiting his imminent death in a hospital ward, while he watches his protege of years, Chandini Gupta, get shot while taking oath as the eighteenth Prime Minister of India on television.<br /><br />Soon after this we find ourselves plunging headlong into the core of the story - the early life of Gangasagar Mishra, his discovery of Chandini in a slum of Kanpur and his subsequent foray into politics. Alternately the story switches back 2300 years into the past, to the era of Dhanananda's misrule and we're shown a young Chanakya vowing to avenge the death of his father Chanak by bringing about the downfall of the oppressive king of Magadh.</i><br /><br /><i>Chanakya's Chant</i> may put you off politics for good (that is, if the unending series of scams and scandals and douchebag politicians of this country haven't done that already). For it repeatedly stresses on the importance of forsaking moral values or ethical considerations, to reach your goal. Both Chanakya and his modern-day avatar, Gangasagar, are depicted as wickedly shrewd, ruthless men, who are hell-bent on achieving success at any cost, allowing nothing to stand in their way.<br />And by the time you reach the end of the book, you will find yourself despising them with a passion as most of their political strategies and decisions, border more on the criminal side rather than just immoral. But then again you will also begrudgingly marvel at the cunning plans they devise.<br /><br />Having read Ashwin Sanghi's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9471031.The_Rozabal_Line" title="The Rozabal Line by Ashwin Sanghi" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rozabal Line</a> quite a few months back, I was aware of his writing style. But when I took up Chanakya's Chant, all thanks to the grace of the Blogadda book-reviews program, I must say I was pleasantly surprised.<br />Unlike <i>The Rozabal Line</i>, this book focuses on weaving a tale of political intrigue without meandering into various subplots or a series of seemingly unconnected stories. Here the events are the key driving factors while detailing and characters become secondary. Although this much is evident that a painstaking amount of research has been put into gathering facts about Chanakya's life and the political environment of our country.<br /><br />The book will bring back memories of history lessons in school when you were taught tales of valor of historical figures like Paurus or Alexander or even Chandragupta Maurya. Although it may also plant the seeds of a nagging suspicion that not all their actions may have been as glorious or awe-inspiring as our history text books suggest.<br /><br />The narration switches back and forth between the two different eras, ending every arc of each story at a point which just heightens the suspense. And one is compelled to read on to find out what happens next.<br />The book can't exactly be called un-put-down-able till the end, but it packs in enough punch to make you want to reach the end as quickly as possible nevertheless.<br /><br />Coming to the negatives, both Chanakya and Gangasagar are portrayed as almost invincible men and their plans are seldom or never thwarted. Not much attention is given to fleshing out the characters of Chandragupta or Chandini. And at the end, you are faced with the bitter realization, that they were perhaps nothing more than mere puppets at the hands of their respective mentors. Cliches, such as pregnancy out of wedlock or sacrificing love in order to realize bigger ambitions, abound. Dialogues are somewhat weak as well and there are hardly any quotes worth remembering. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Certain incidents such as the honorable home minister of India, shooting a civilian with his own hands, without batting an eyelid, seemed incredulous to me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />And what's most regrettable of all, none of the characters leave a lasting impression on you.<br /><br />But even so, <i>Chanakya's Chant</i> remains a well-written political thriller. I give it a 3.5 stars out of 5 more 'cause of the fact that it successfully kept me hooked from the beginning till the end.<br /><br /><i>**A review copy was kindly forwarded to me by blogadda in exchange for an honest review**</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6338608994737827961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_443491448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/443491448" />
    <a title="Rajat TWIT" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8571445-rajat-twit"><img alt="Rajat TWIT" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483729035p2/8571445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/443491448?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rajat TWIT" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rajat TWIT" href="/user/show/8571445-rajat-twit">Rajat TWIT</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443491448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2333834249471726038">Starting with the wrong political map of India, this book had given me enough reasons to hate it. I wanted to stop by the time I was on 100th page but carried on just to observe how irritating this book might go. And it topped the list of the most stupid book I have ever read. Businessmen of Mauryan age are shown SHAMPOOING but in reality, the process CHAMPI (etymology of shampoo has this word in centre) was evolved during Mughal reigns and term/method of Shampoo came in existence in 18th centur</span>
  <span id="freeText2333834249471726038" style="display:none">Starting with the wrong political map of India, this book had given me enough reasons to hate it. I wanted to stop by the time I was on 100th page but carried on just to observe how irritating this book might go. And it topped the list of the most stupid book I have ever read. Businessmen of Mauryan age are shown SHAMPOOING but in reality, the process CHAMPI (etymology of shampoo has this word in centre) was evolved during Mughal reigns and term/method of Shampoo came in existence in 18th century. Chankya is shown using language which is not only filthy but extremely down market. Imagine a scholar of such repute using hindi equivalent of terms like Rat’s ass, Horse’s shit, Camel’s fart. Agreed that the book is in English, but then also the revered academician, master strategician and renowned pandit will never ever use such foul language.<br />And not only words spoken by chankaya’s character but the whole book’s language is very shabby and distasteful. You will find feeling of deja vu in many expressions and idioms. Redundancy made it unbearable to read. Usage of good words is limited and there is no depth in the characters of story. The characters are so shallow that you will feel no connection with any of them, even the lead characters of both stories. Time frame of current story has got many irregularities and it was hilarious to read the way Gangasagar makes plans to introduce Ikrambhai in politics and makes him CM of UP in the very next elections. And he decides who will be next Prime Minister almost by will according to the situation and never gets any trouble in executing his plans. Although starting his career as a simpleton guy he manages to get influential friends in US and Britain and in high posts of all important departments. He grooms and makes the fate of student leaders and manages to put them in such posts like Governor of RBI and blah blah blah……… and just read the extremely abrupt end on Chankya’s story. It’s so confusing that you will be left wondering whatever the hell happened.<br />Usage of wonderful quotes and saying by great people are the only point to be lauded, but then in this age of information it is rarely a problem to read such quotes. We have enough self-help books in case you are not net savvy! Single star rating that I gave is just because of these quotes.<br />This book is cheaper than the B grade Bollywood movie. No wonders its heavy sales has made UTV to buy the rights of this book. Because as said by Charles McCabe (also used in this book): any clod can have the facts, having an opinion is an art!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2333834249471726038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_410600278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410600278" />
    <a title="Anand " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8957806-anand"><img alt="Anand " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335092693p2/8957806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410600278?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anand " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anand " href="/user/show/8957806-anand">Anand </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410600278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4872977630637404104">This is Sanghi's second novel I read, after his more recent 'The Krishna Key'. Frankly, I was disappointed. Average ratings suggested that Chanakya's Chant is better received than Krishna Key, and it was with that expectation and excitement that I purchased this. But, as I mentioned, this is disappointing.<br/><br/>The historical part depicting Chanakya is relatively grippier, but the modern day narrative is too contrived, naive and amateurish. The modern tale reads more like an ordinary Bollywood script </span>
  <span id="freeText4872977630637404104" style="display:none">This is Sanghi's second novel I read, after his more recent 'The Krishna Key'. Frankly, I was disappointed. Average ratings suggested that Chanakya's Chant is better received than Krishna Key, and it was with that expectation and excitement that I purchased this. But, as I mentioned, this is disappointing.<br /><br />The historical part depicting Chanakya is relatively grippier, but the modern day narrative is too contrived, naive and amateurish. The modern tale reads more like an ordinary Bollywood script with politics as a background and scheming, dirty, evil, corrupt characters for the various roles. More often than not the quotes, sentences and dialogues are a simplistic and literal translation of spoken Hindi into English, which leaves a lot to be desired. Add to that numerous, purportedly high wisdom one-liners to be found in almost every paragraph, all of which make Gangasagar (the modern 'Chanakya' in this novel) sound too unreal. However cunning and shrewd a person may be, I doubt they converse in such an unreal manner through quoting quotes every second breath.<br /><br />Further, there are too many sub-plots and small incidents that keep getting narrated, making the plot very confusing and complex. As it is the reader has to be keep track of two parallel times, and to add to that numerous complexities is unnecessary. Things could have been kept a lot simpler, and leaner, and the book therefore ought to have been about a 100-150 pages shorter. <br /><br />While I like the overall idea and concept behind this novel, the treatment, narrative and the language are a big let down when judged in the context of the high expectations set for this novel from an author who clearly is vastly gifted and different from the ordinary. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4872977630637404104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sudha Shashwati" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sudha Shashwati" href="/user/show/6785558-sudha-shashwati">Sudha Shashwati</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268967546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14541343671431770628">There can be stories we don't agree with, but the manner of story telling can make us fall in love with it and the same story can go on to remain etched in our memory for a long time. That's the beauty of 'Chanakya's Chant' and the genius of Ashwin Sanghi.<br/><br/>This book did to me what 'Godfather' had done a month back. As a person, there was no way that I could appreciate the 'wisdom' being propagated by either Chanakya or his modern avatar Professor Gangasagar Mishra- that ends justify the means, th</span>
  <span id="freeText14541343671431770628" style="display:none">There can be stories we don't agree with, but the manner of story telling can make us fall in love with it and the same story can go on to remain etched in our memory for a long time. That's the beauty of 'Chanakya's Chant' and the genius of Ashwin Sanghi.<br /><br />This book did to me what 'Godfather' had done a month back. As a person, there was no way that I could appreciate the 'wisdom' being propagated by either Chanakya or his modern avatar Professor Gangasagar Mishra- that ends justify the means, that all politics is dirty, that revealing your true feelings never serves any good- in short that you have to suppress everything that is human in you and be consumed by the ultimate aim. Yet I couldn't help appreciating the same 'wisdom' as a psychology student. The sheer intellect and raw cunning of the both the kingmakers began to impress me from the word go and the breath-taking pace at which it ran compelled me to finish it in 2 settings flat.<br />Anybody who has a fair amount of interest in politics or historical/mythological fiction will love this book. Even if she/he doesn't agree with what it espouses.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5346186960563363086">The book has two stories- one takes place at around 2000 years ago (about chanakya) and the other about the current politicians and the political scenario. – More or less both are same.<br/>The current story reveals about the politicians, how they get elected, and how low they will go to get elected, etcetera. Those who have the habit of reading\hearing the news daily (that too during election time) you can </span>
  <span id="freeText5346186960563363086" style="display:none">The book has two stories- one takes place at around 2000 years ago (about chanakya) and the other about the current politicians and the political scenario. – More or less both are same.<br />The current story reveals about the politicians, how they get elected, and how low they will go to get elected, etcetera. While reading this (current scenario part), I feel more like reading a newspaper than a book. Those who have the habit of reading\hearing the news daily (that too during election time) you can skip these chapters and continue with the old chanakya version. There isn’t anything new to tell about this version of story. <br />About Chanakya’s era: I haven’t read anything about chanakya (just a single line in my history subject in school, mentioning he is a prominent member in Chandragupta’s reign) before starting this book. So I had a very high opinion on him but now I’m very much disappointed. I have read some other historical fictions before in Tamil written by kalki. I used to love those books. After finishing those books sometimes I feel like ‘Wow!! We were born in a superb country even though now our own politicians have destroyed it’. The characters in those books will do anything with dignity to keep up their promise where as here in this book they will do anything (lying, murdering and never keeping their promise) just to get something for themselves. After reading this book I’m thinking <i>Oh my God!! Even 2000 years ago our rulers are just like our current politicians?</i> I don’t like the thought and so I don’t like the book...</span>

<div id="review_661675195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661675195" />
    <a title="Sushmitha Kanukurthi " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3405656-sushmitha-kanukurthi"><img alt="Sushmitha Kanukurthi " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347225697p2/3405656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661675195?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sushmitha Kanukurthi " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sushmitha Kanukurthi " href="/user/show/3405656-sushmitha-kanukurthi">Sushmitha Kanukurthi </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661675195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17446303076117812232">Two months - that's how long it took me to finish this book. In all my reading life, never have I struggled through a book as much as I did with this one. Chanakya's chant, written by Ashwin Sanghi, is a let down on all fronts - The story never seems to take off, the writing is appalling at best (and that is still paying a compliment to the writer), the plot seems ill thought out and what's worse, it is even more horribly executed. In all, this book is a disaster. <br/> <br/>For the (fortunately) uninitia</span>
  <span id="freeText17446303076117812232" style="display:none">Two months - that's how long it took me to finish this book. In all my reading life, never have I struggled through a book as much as I did with this one. Chanakya's chant, written by Ashwin Sanghi, is a let down on all fronts - The story never seems to take off, the writing is appalling at best (and that is still paying a compliment to the writer), the plot seems ill thought out and what's worse, it is even more horribly executed. In all, this book is a disaster. <br /> <br />For the (fortunately) uninitiated, Chanakya's Chant is a story that's set in two different eras - one of Chanakya from 350 BC and another of Pandit Gangasagar Mishra (PGM), set in present day India. The supposedly parallel stories of the two protagonits have only one thing in common - both Chankya and PGM are consumed by their desire for power. But that's where the similarities end. While Chanakya's story requires nothing more than referencing historical textbooks on the subject, PGM's story is a shabbily written collection of all the scams that have plagued India over the past decade. One cannot fail to see the similarities between the telecom scam in the book and the 2G scam in India. And this is just one of the many scams that the writer (un)successfully tries to pass off under the guise original story telling. What makes you squirm with every page though, is the style of writing. It is horrific to see jokes and one liners that you did not even enjoy as a teenager, occupy space in the book. Lines such as "we all know that children in the dark cause accidents and accidents in the back seat cause children" are an indication of how mediocre writing is accompanied by absolute lack of creativity. The protagonists seem to be like demi-gods who can get anything they want just by wishing for it. Towards the end of the book, one tends to get the feeling that Ashwin Sanghi is trying to glorify all that is wrong with the Indian Political system today and nothing can depress the reader more than that.<br /><br />I could go on and on but I am going to end on this note - if you really believe that reading provides you with the much needed intellectual nourishment or are even looking for light hearted entertainment, avoid this one like the plague! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17446303076117812232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_615959530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615959530" />
    <a title="Abhinav" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10051075-abhinav"><img alt="Abhinav" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388563530p2/10051075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615959530?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abhinav" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abhinav" href="/user/show/10051075-abhinav">Abhinav</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=2013-reading-saga">2013-reading-saga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=popular-fiction">popular-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=love-cum-like-zyada">love-cum-like-zyada</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615959530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16503972570777193317">And with this book, I've finished reading all of Ashwin Sanghi's works. While I do not certainly consider that as some sort of achievement, it feels good to know that you've read all the books of some author, no matter how good or bad he is.<br/><br/>So, coming to the immensely popular 'Chanakya's Chant', a political thriller set in two different ages - in ancient Bharat & in the present day. Sanghi exults in using the 'history repeats itself' theme in all his novels & this one is no different, although I</span>
  <span id="freeText16503972570777193317" style="display:none">And with this book, I've finished reading all of Ashwin Sanghi's works. While I do not certainly consider that as some sort of achievement, it feels good to know that you've read all the books of some author, no matter how good or bad he is.<br /><br />So, coming to the immensely popular 'Chanakya's Chant', a political thriller set in two different ages - in ancient Bharat &amp; in the present day. Sanghi exults in using the 'history repeats itself' theme in all his novels &amp; this one is no different, although I must say he uses it rather well this time.<br /><br />The plot opens in a hospital ward at Kanpur as an aging Pandit Gangasagar Mishra watches his protege Chandini Gupta get shot moments after taking oath as the Prime Minister of India. Then we are zapped back in time to two &amp; a half millennia ago, where we see how Vishnugupta sees his beloved father mercilessly killed by the king of Magadha &amp; how he christens himself 'Chanakya' while swearing revenge. The tale keeps oscillating between these two different time periods as Sanghi traces a pattern (that's what this book is about, after all) in the rise of both these men, who eventually turn out to be master political strategists &amp; ultimate kingmakers of their era - Chanakya mentoring Chandragupta Maurya &amp; Gangasagar tutoring the beautiful slum-child Chandini Gupta.<br /><br />What this book very well explores is how cold, cruel, cunning &amp; calculating individuals both Chanakya &amp; Gangasagar are - who will use the dirtiest tricks in the manual to achieve their ulterior motives. As a result, the characterisation of the protagonists is very good indeed, but the other key characters in this book seem to be mere puppets in their hands (which they are, actually). This kind of manipulation reminded me of Sidney Sheldon's bestselling novel 'Master of the Game', but the comparison is totally meant as a compliment.<br /><br />Despite the author liberally distorting historical accounts from the time of Chanakya for the purpose of storytelling, I found it gripping throughout. What I also liked is how Sanghi takes inspiration from recent events in India's political sphere to create the present day scenario which Gangasagar considers his battleground.<br /><br />The cliched characters, poor dialogue (sorry Mr. Sanghi, but supposedly 'witty' statements do not always come across as witty) &amp; a couple of unbelievable sequences in the latter half of the book (one being an action sequence feat. the honourable Home Minister of India, reminding you of mindless Bollywood masala potboilers) mar this erstwhile engaging thriller. I really wish that the author had stuck to telling us the good story he had on his hands rather than trying to make it more 'filmable', if you can call that.<br /><br />Still, Ashwin Sanghi manages to produce his best work till date in 'Chanakya's Chant' &amp; I can see why it managed to rule the bestseller charts for over a year. My rating is 3.5 stars &amp; upwards for this riveting political thriller (extra marks for the beautiful cover art!) &amp; it is certainly one of the better books I've come across in Indian popular fiction. Recommended for those who like their dose of thrills with a splash of history in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16503972570777193317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText6013280957477865590" style="display:none">When i watched the video above, i expected the book to be a powerful one, not in the sense of writing, but in the strength of the main characters. <div id="review_144415744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144415744" />
    <a title="Salvadesswaran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3656234-salvadesswaran"><img alt="Salvadesswaran" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144415744?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Salvadesswaran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Salvadesswaran" href="/user/show/3656234-salvadesswaran">Salvadesswaran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3656234-salvadesswaran?shelf=home-library">home-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144415744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15354825147195229172">From: <a href='http://queasyquagmire.wordpress.com/2011/01/29/book-review-chanakyas-chant/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review at my blog</a><br/><br/>Chanakya’s Chant is Ashwin Sanghi’s second novel after The Rozabal Line. It revolves around the life of a Pandit who emerges as a modern day Chanakya.<br/><br/>The style is similar to his debut, linking modern events to those that occurred two millennia ago. We have seen this style many times, flipping between two parallel events – only here, the parallel events are from long ago.<br/><br/>A Pandit from Kanpur with financial banking from a merchant and manpower from a Muslim strongman manages</span>
  <span id="freeText15354825147195229172" style="display:none">From: <a href="http://queasyquagmire.wordpress.com/2011/01/29/book-review-chanakyas-chant/" rel="nofollow noopener">Review at my blog</a><br /><br />Chanakya’s Chant is Ashwin Sanghi’s second novel after The Rozabal Line. It revolves around the life of a Pandit who emerges as a modern day Chanakya.<br /><br />The style is similar to his debut, linking modern events to those that occurred two millennia ago. We have seen this style many times, flipping between two parallel events – only here, the parallel events are from long ago.<br /><br />A Pandit from Kanpur with financial banking from a merchant and manpower from a Muslim strongman manages to unite the people of the city and assume political power. He makes his disciple becomes the most powerful woman in the country, just as Chanakya enthroned Chandragupta Maurya. As he develops the plot, Sanghi touches upon many issues in modern India – religious friction, corruption and the like. He is clearly inspired by real world events such as the tussle between the Ambani brothers, cash for votes, the fodder scam and the 2G scam(yes, that one too!). There are several instances where the media is cleverly used by devious politicians – #MediaMafia, anyone?<br /><br />The description of Uttar Pradesh, I cannot comment upon for I have confined myself to Tamil Nadu most of my life. However, the unhygienic conditions and the slum might very well fit into any large town in India. One could draw parallels between the two central characters and the BSP in Uttar Pradesh too. A minor quibble I see is that Sanghi has portrayed the Keralite as talking English with a funny accent. He cannot be further from the truth here – I know many Keralites who have a neutral accent; I haven’t seen a person speak with the accent he writes. There are several quotes that are wrongly attributed to Chanakya, but the Acknowledgements &amp; References section makes this clear.<br /><br />I do not have a large appetite for historical thrillers, and so I cannot compare this work with many others. It might seem at the outset that Sanghi is developing into a desi Dan Brown, given his penchant for history. I hope we can expect a deviation from this genre in his future work.<br /><br />There is a lot of gore – and not all of it is blood. There are several descriptions of coitus and mutilations that are not really necessary – just page filling material. There is too much profanity on show too. The book could have been shorter by a fifth, and even then I doubt it’d have been a gripping read. However, it is a pleasing way to pass a lazy Saturday afternoon. It is quite entertaining and the history is not as wrong as in many other in its genre. I was expecting better, especially after The Rozabal Line, but Sanghi has not disappointed either.<br /><br />Plus: A good plot, Nice real-life parallels,Enjoyable<br /><br />Minus: Too much page filler, Stereotyping<br /><br />Rating: 6.5/10<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15354825147195229172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156535066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12673888552239341116">This book was a replacement by my brother for "Thousand Splendid Suns" as he lost it. The former book is one of my favorites. I can't say I liked Chanakya chant as much as 'TSS', but both are divergent from each other so who was I to judge? <br/> I started reading this one just because it was quite interesting from the excerpt. First of all, you don't have to like a story to like a book and that is something I understood after reading this one. Gangasagar was like Chanakya's in many ways but not in a</span>
  <span id="freeText12673888552239341116" style="display:none">This book was a replacement by my brother for "Thousand Splendid Suns" as he lost it. The former book is one of my favorites. I can't say I liked Chanakya chant as much as 'TSS', but both are divergent from each other so who was I to judge? <br /> I started reading this one just because it was quite interesting from the excerpt. First of all, you don't have to like a story to like a book and that is something I understood after reading this one. Gangasagar was like Chanakya's in many ways but not in all and so was the case with the story. The story is gripping, entertaining and different.I won't lie so yeah there were times when I wanted to beat the crap out of some characters but I still couldn't stop reading it. I couldn't help it. <br /><br /><br />It was also my first thriller book by an Indian author, YES YOU GUESSED RIGHT! I READ THIS BOOK A LONG TIME AGO AND I LOVED IT.I had tried reading stories (genre- romance) before by some Indian authors but i couldn't complete them.They were just so dull and uninteresting. Then, I bought Krishna Key and so came other Indian authors in my life. Right now, I am completing Amish's other series.I love his books!The Shiva Series rocks!<br /><br />But this book will always have a special place in my life!<br /><br />Five stars!<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText10521905122150208444" style="display:none">"A free society is a society where it is safe to be unpopular." -- Adlai Stevenson<br /><br />The quote is from this book, and there are several such quotes in the book interwoven in dialogues of characters. The book is fast paced thriller, which I liked but yet I give it three stars because I am no fan of 'Chanakya'. Chanakya stands on the opposite end of moral stands of Mahatma Gandhi who said bad means are not justified to achieve anything (good or bad). Whereas Chanakyra represents either too ordinary person or at best pessimist who says it is not possible to achieve good without committing some sins. </span>

<div id="review_474212429" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474212429" />
    <a title="Neha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2327087-neha"><img alt="Neha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593193903p2/2327087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474212429?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neha" href="/user/show/2327087-neha">Neha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327087-neha?shelf=g-asia-india">g-asia-india</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327087-neha?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327087-neha?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2327087-neha?shelf=history-myth-fiction">history-myth-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474212429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5953085789269690365">Indian fiction is in evolutionary phase. Moving from the old school NRI authors like Rushdie, Chitra Banerjee, Jhumpa and Naipaul writing on their native for the foreign audience, to the new breed of indigenous authors like Chetan Bhagat, Anuja Chauhan experimenting with middle class subjects, to intelligent thinking man's writers like Manu Joseph and Arvind Adiga, and the historic/mythological fiction writers like Amish and Ashwin Sanghi. <br/><br/>So it was inevitable for me to pick one Ashwin Sanghi bo</span>
  <span id="freeText5953085789269690365" style="display:none">Indian fiction is in evolutionary phase. Moving from the old school NRI authors like Rushdie, Chitra Banerjee, Jhumpa and Naipaul writing on their native for the foreign audience, to the new breed of indigenous authors like Chetan Bhagat, Anuja Chauhan experimenting with middle class subjects, to intelligent thinking man's writers like Manu Joseph and Arvind Adiga, and the historic/mythological fiction writers like Amish and Ashwin Sanghi. <br /><br />So it was inevitable for me to pick one Ashwin Sanghi book. This one came highly recommended, especially Chanakya is an intriguing character, his economic and political understanding has been the root of all of Indian History and current political scenario. The man was a visionary and has influenced the ancient history in such a deep manner that it resonates till date.<br /><br />Ashwin Sanghi starts off well with a very strong storyline and characters, shifting between historic journey of Chanakya and his protégé Chandragupta and the re-creation of Gangasagar and Chandini in the current times. The former was handled well by the author probably because it was retelling of the history the way it has been written and re-written over times. <br /><br />The real skill of the author would be in his ability to re-create it again in the modern times, but here is where I found a slag in author's handling of the subject. Where Gangasagar proved to be great Chanakya, Chandini failed to impress. He could have very well picked up any random girl rather than focus on grooming Chandini since childhood. I understand it was to be a girl protégé as per the ancient prophecy, but then again she seemed like a puppet in hands of Gangasagar rather than an intelligent thinking woman. <br /><br />Other than that the book tries to club two stories and two lifetimes in a short version, so speed and pace sometimes lead to short cut solutions and easy maneuvers by the author. Overall a good attempt. Here are a few lines from the book which I liked:<br /><br /><i>There cannot be a country without people, and there is no kingdom without a country. It's the people who constitude a kingdom; like a barren cow, a kingdom without people yields nothing. <br /><br />Worry is like a Rocking chair, it keeps you busy but gets you nowhere.<br /><br />A free society is one where it's safe to be unpopular, but then, freedom of speech also carries with it the freedom not to listen. <br /><br />Remember that it's often easier to get forgiveness rather than permission.<br /><br />Wise men think all they say, fools say all they think. <br /><br />Bravery is simply being the only one who knows that you're afraid.<br /><br />Birds don't build nests on fruitless trees, whores have no love for poor men, and citizens don't obey a powerless king! </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5953085789269690365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16231498480870272183" style="display:none">Adi Shakti, Namo Namah<br />Sarab Shakti, Namo Namah<br />Prithum Bhagvati, Namo Namah<br />Kundalini Mata Shakti<br />Mata Shakti, Namo Namah<br /><br />-Chanakya's chant<br /><br /><br />Before reading this book,I didn't know that a book about some political genius guru can be this interesting. It totally blew my mind. Started reading during my train journey and couldn't stop till it was finished.<br /><br />Author has nailed it while portraying ancient and present day politics in India. Rise of Chanakya from a simple and talented Brahmin kid to becoming greatest kingmaker who ever lived, couldn't have been written in a more intense and gripping story tale. Complex situations,cunning solutions by Chanakya,full of action implementation by his disciples and to the point results ,make this book a must read for all politics lovers.<br /><br />Ashwin sanghi leaves no stones unturned while scripting the story of Pt. Gangasagar Mishra , the modern day avatar of Chanakya. Gangasagar,a brahmin from Kanpur,uses his sharp and cunning intelligence to make the career of his protegee Chandini Gupta. This story of modern day politics,made me think twice about the actual events that are happening in Indian politics. All the twists and turns were feeling like deja vu.<br /><br />A must read indeed. </span>

  <span id="freeText7937469057361866798" style="display:none">As every election unfolds, media and so-called sephologists go to a tizzy over someone whom they call The Chanakya. Then, as the dust settles over the landscape, either the supposed kingmaker is hailed, or the poor sod gets roasted as a con job.<br />But what about the real deal?<br />What if a modern incarnation of Chanakya, working with the sole aim of uniting the nation under one ruler, decides to enter the game?<br />This novel is a case study with respect to that scenario.<br />It's also the finest make-believe biographical fiction about Chanakya, that we have had.<br />Above all, it's a gripping political thriller that takes us on an utterly amoral, yet hugely entertaining ride.<br />Recommended, but please, don't try to put ALL those maxims into usage.<br />Like potent medicine, those lessons are to be taken one at a time.</span>

<div id="review_711510335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711510335" />
    <a title="Nagesh Kumar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23368893-nagesh-kumar"><img alt="Nagesh Kumar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377366612p2/23368893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711510335?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nagesh Kumar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nagesh Kumar" href="/user/show/23368893-nagesh-kumar">Nagesh Kumar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/18050341-chanakya-s-chant">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711510335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11152497681563445424"> I am sorry to disappoint you. But please blame Dan Brown for the same.<br/><br/>I am talking of his new offering: Inferno, a novel based on Dante’s works, artifacts with mysteries; throw in a Biomedical weapon, a deadly virus to set off the hero Langdon saddled with a short-term amnesia as he stumbles though the besieged Florence city ( Alas! This hero has not seen Ghajini, so he is not as smart as Aamir Khan!) aided by a bald lady Doctor on a wild goose chase, all the while ducking from Military Police.</span>
  <span id="freeText11152497681563445424" style="display:none"> I am sorry to disappoint you. But please blame Dan Brown for the same.<br /><br />I am talking of his new offering: Inferno, a novel based on Dante’s works, artifacts with mysteries; throw in a Biomedical weapon, a deadly virus to set off the hero Langdon saddled with a short-term amnesia as he stumbles though the besieged Florence city ( Alas! This hero has not seen Ghajini, so he is not as smart as Aamir Khan!) aided by a bald lady Doctor on a wild goose chase, all the while ducking from Military Police..<br /><br />Confusing enough? But wait.. The assured thrills are there, and so are the clever twists at the end of each Chapter through which the author takes us on a nail-biting and often puzzling chase covering Italy and Turkey with the couple ducking from bullets, à la Jason Bourne cum James Bond.<br /><br />Without revealing more as spoilers, I will answer your questions…<br /><br />Was it Good?: ..haa….hmm..Yeah, but….sort of…<br />What was not Good?: When the end becomes impotent and unproductive, you come away unsatisfied.. Like what was this entire futile chase about?<br />Now to decipher the last two italicized words above (Sorry, Dan Brown, you are getting to me), you will have to read the book to ‘the end’.<br /><br /> The Chanakaya’s Chant is the second one of his novels<br /><br />This is a supposed to be a Historical and Political drama , one thread on the famous Chanakya , the wily, intelligent but crooked, smart but cunning, successful but cruel Brahmin guide and philosopher who has a personal vendetta agenda to settle with the present Magadha king.<br />He plots , confuses and creates a holy mess in warfare among neighboring kings and their states to get what he wants…He wants to install his protégé Chandragupta Maurya in place..<br />The second thread of story running parallels is that of modern day politician/ king maker called<br />Gangasagar who does the same with modern political parties, forges alliances with crooked mine owners, real estate businessmen, hijras, “honey traps” and assassins to make and break alliances that he wants in power.<br />He also has his puppet PM candidate who he wants to establish in Delhi…<br /> How things turn out for the original Chanakya and this modern chanakya , Gangasagar is the rest of the story.<br />It is Ok, its like a new type of story line mixing History and present day politics together . It is not very complimentary on Great Brahmin Chanakya as we know him; in fact author tries his best to make him detestable and as villainous as possible.<br />The writing style is not so great. It is mere hype that this author is hailed as 'Indian Dan Brown' (of Da Vinci code fame)<br /><br />This book is supposed to be made into a Hindi movie by UTV.<br />Rating: 3/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="11152497681563445424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_248884289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248884289" />
    <a title="Hrishikesh Bharali" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4772227-hrishikesh-bharali"><img alt="Hrishikesh Bharali" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536509907p2/4772227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248884289?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hrishikesh Bharali" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hrishikesh Bharali" href="/user/show/4772227-hrishikesh-bharali">Hrishikesh Bharali</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248884289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12261832828391811634">I wouldn't have picked up this book if it wasn't for the title "Chanakya's Chant",that caught my attention.I had always been in awe of the great economist and politician in ancient India, also known as Kautilya.His work "Arthashastra" is one of its kind.So with that in mind,and the recommendations from the likes of Shashi Tharoor,a man of intellect, and Amish Tripathi,whose Shiva Trilogy has kept me spell-bound,made me go for this book.<br/>Far from being a religious treatise of Chanakya,as one would</span>
  <span id="freeText12261832828391811634" style="display:none">I wouldn't have picked up this book if it wasn't for the title "Chanakya's Chant",that caught my attention.I had always been in awe of the great economist and politician in ancient India, also known as Kautilya.His work "Arthashastra" is one of its kind.So with that in mind,and the recommendations from the likes of Shashi Tharoor,a man of intellect, and Amish Tripathi,whose Shiva Trilogy has kept me spell-bound,made me go for this book.<br />Far from being a religious treatise of Chanakya,as one would guess from its title,the book runs parallel stories of the lives of two king-makers Chanakya,in ancient India and Pt.Gangasagar Mishra,in present day India,masters in the game of politics and economics unravelling a world of political and economical master play; doing what they do best-a rich display of their war-craft.<br />The narration recounts the early life span of Chanakya, right from his childhood till he succeeded in his ultimate objective-unification of Bharat (India) and re-installation of Chandragupta Maurya on the throne of Magadha;keeping in tandem is a present day story of Pt.Gangasagar Mishra who has a similar game-plan in mind-to make Chandini Gupta, the Prime Minister of India. Both are ambushed in their missions by hurdles which they overcame through a series of maze of lie,deception,power,money etc. with a view at the greater good that comes with the end result-which somehow reminds me of Krishna's sayings to Arjun during the epic battle of Mahabharata.<br />The book is acutely well-written with apt quotes thrown in between which makes it a very pleasant experience.However,I strongly recommend against picking up this book for anyone who isn't so drawn into politics or economics for that matter.There is every possibility that the game of political warfare might bore you out and throw you into a deep slumber.Otherwise,go for it at the earliest! It's totally worth the space in your book-shelf!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12261832828391811634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Chahat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5394459-chahat"><img alt="Chahat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334920215p2/5394459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/285881083?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chahat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chahat" href="/user/show/5394459-chahat">Chahat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285881083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9999077525578339292">A very thoughtfully crafted novel which draws amazing parallel between history and contemporary. With mind blowing one-liners and quotations, Ashwin Sanghi has brought out a very descriptive character sketch of Chanakya's persona. Also, he has very aptly portrayed how the human psyche works irrespective of the era. How even the minutest of differences can be exploited , how major differences can be created with the know-how of the structure and how a battle can be won without bloodshed. At some </span>
  <span id="freeText9999077525578339292" style="display:none">A very thoughtfully crafted novel which draws amazing parallel between history and contemporary. With mind blowing one-liners and quotations, Ashwin Sanghi has brought out a very descriptive character sketch of Chanakya's persona. Also, he has very aptly portrayed how the human psyche works irrespective of the era. How even the minutest of differences can be exploited , how major differences can be created with the know-how of the structure and how a battle can be won without bloodshed. At some point, it is so brutal and savage that it makes your mind doubt whether the protagonist is the hero or the villain but then one has to settle for that he is just the chess player and that the other characters are merely the pawns. You can’t feel sorry for even the queen if you are rooting for the king to win. The novel conveyed the feelings of revenge, a channelled anger , farsightedness and an ultimate goal of a united Bharat by Chanakya in the past and equally dedicated aim of Gangasagar to install Chandini as the Prime Minister of India.The sudden twists and turns, the well planned strategies, the extreme planning and the out-of-the-box flabbergasting ideas would definitely make up to be an excellent movie script.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9999077525578339292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357254418?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer8023480571237102368">There are certain stories where we would be awestruck with either in the language part and some times the vice versa i.e with the story line. I found this particular pick , excelling in both the terms. The author has did a deep research in bringing out this book. Initially I thought, It was just a historical fiction. But the comparitive writing and linking the old chanakya's methodology with the modern day Ganagasagar's , the author has shown his due diligence in bringing out the story line of t</span>
  <span id="freeText8023480571237102368" style="display:none">There are certain stories where we would be awestruck with either in the language part and some times the vice versa i.e with the story line. I found this particular pick , excelling in both the terms. The author has did a deep research in bringing out this book. Initially I thought, It was just a historical fiction. But the comparitive writing and linking the old chanakya's methodology with the modern day Ganagasagar's , the author has shown his due diligence in bringing out the story line of the book. Never a page, I lost my interest in reading, though the book is some what bigger. In my watch and experience of reading certain books of this genre, most of the authors are so inclined towards the story part and some where the readers will be struck with the fictional part and not a lesson will be learnt or realised at the end. But reading wise, you will find as if you were in a heaven in those kind of books. But here, there is a moral in every episode of the story. There is a rationale behind every other scene.<br /><br />Of all the stuffs, the punch lines of both chanakya's and Ganagsagar's are very catchy. The following is my favourite.<br /><br />"You should keep your enemies closer than your friends".</span>

<div id="review_917091435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
