    <a title="Ankita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27677971-ankita"><img alt="Ankita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389717434p2/27677971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/917091435?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ankita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ankita" href="/user/show/27677971-ankita">Ankita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Nook 2940012393791" href="/book/show/11031448-chanakya-s-chant">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer917091435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer911796439552207940">I'd actually like to rate it a 3.5<br/><br/>Reading Chanakya's Chant is like reading two novels at once. And obviously so since it narrates two stories - that of Chanakya and a Pandit Gangasagar Mishra in modern India.<br/><br/>It's quite interesting to see how the author re-enacts the events of the ancient Scholar's life. They may be fictitious but while reading I was quite compelled to believe otherwise. However, at times it does feel a bit mythical and far-fetched. The politics played by Mishraji in the Modern I</span>
  <span id="freeText911796439552207940" style="display:none">I'd actually like to rate it a 3.5<br /><br />Reading Chanakya's Chant is like reading two novels at once. And obviously so since it narrates two stories - that of Chanakya and a Pandit Gangasagar Mishra in modern India.<br /><br />It's quite interesting to see how the author re-enacts the events of the ancient Scholar's life. They may be fictitious but while reading I was quite compelled to believe otherwise. However, at times it does feel a bit mythical and far-fetched. The politics played by Mishraji in the Modern India parallel is quite interesting in the beginning. I could say I was a bit awed since I don't follow politics very actively and the events that play out were refreshing to read. However, as the story progressed, it grew too 'Rajniti'-ish, Bollywood-style.<br /><br />Both timelines progressed at their own pace. Chanakya's story crawled whereas Mishraji's story progressed quickly. The (slightly) sentimental ending was quite a surprise.<br /><br />Nevertheless, an engaging read! I quite enjoyed the ride. Some of you might find it a bit heavy but that's when Chanakya steps in and takes you on a different course. <br /><br />A must read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="911796439552207940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_337920288" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337920288" />
    <a title="Abishek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9827780-abishek"><img alt="Abishek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338184944p2/9827780.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337920288?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abishek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abishek" href="/user/show/9827780-abishek">Abishek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337920288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7928117814115913022">Nicely written piece of Indian fiction. Out of the two stories, i found the "present-day" story more gripping. The political fore-play inter-wined with the corporate greed is depicted nicely. Although all the incidents are too co-incidental to happen to the same parties, i am sure they occur in the dirty world of politics. The money making schemes and scandals were mildly impressive. However, the victories are easily achieved. It would have been really good if the author stressed the character's</span>
  <span id="freeText7928117814115913022" style="display:none">Nicely written piece of Indian fiction. Out of the two stories, i found the "present-day" story more gripping. The political fore-play inter-wined with the corporate greed is depicted nicely. Although all the incidents are too co-incidental to happen to the same parties, i am sure they occur in the dirty world of politics. The money making schemes and scandals were mildly impressive. However, the victories are easily achieved. It would have been really good if the author stressed the character's rise to power rather than his efficiency in using it. <br /><br />i definitely liked the writing style. The little snippets bringing all the wheels to motion towards a big story-twister kept me (mildly suffering from attention deficiency :-)) going through the pages. The attention to detail shows that a lot of research is done.<br /><br />Having said that,the title made me buy this book. I was interested in Chanakya's story and his learning and teachings about economics. sadly this book did not even come close to this expectation.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7928117814115913022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/797795427?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23282535-vikram-choudhari?shelf=indian-writing">indian-writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797795427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17257622186290570284">Chanakya’s Chant by Ashwin Sanghi gives its readers a look into two parallel worlds that are tied together by the intelligence of the main protagonists. The first story is set in 340 BC, when a young Brahmin man, fueled by the death of his father, vows revenge against the king and overthrows his rule by bringing in Chandragupta Maurya, the first emperor of the Maurya Dynasty. <br/>Then the scene then shifts to modern day India, where Gangasagar Mishra leads his life as a nonentity – until he decides </span>
  <span id="freeText17257622186290570284" style="display:none">Chanakya’s Chant by Ashwin Sanghi gives its readers a look into two parallel worlds that are tied together by the intelligence of the main protagonists. The first story is set in 340 BC, when a young Brahmin man, fueled by the death of his father, vows revenge against the king and overthrows his rule by bringing in Chandragupta Maurya, the first emperor of the Maurya Dynasty. <br />Then the scene then shifts to modern day India, where Gangasagar Mishra leads his life as a nonentity – until he decides to groom an ambitious girl from Kanpur into India’s prime minister. The book takes readers on a joyride through Chanakya’s cold and calculating moves. <br />Ashwin takes us into working of every major govt. organisation may it be PMO or IB just like Dan Brown did in his every other book. Looking forward to read The Rozabel line as well.. <br />Must read..<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17257622186290570284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FC4UZmhBpUKbcLngYUSr6hwa0FQtpbiPX5s6yRaLB3TXa+IBno8K3CS+/u4+qBd2OkeS1T8Ddn5BHIq96Txh2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gEQf3JhsjitkAbEyhpo0t4jsMLF6uwHYwDPPuzXVvApDAem7bqIhtdvP9jzZdogrrrFyMGgdzynetH/PymLapw==')})
  }
//]]>

In what modern Indians mistakenly call the Indus Valley Civilisation. The inhabitants of that period called it the land of Meluha a near perfect empire created many centuries earlier by Lord Ram, one of the greatest monarchs that ever lived. This once proud empire and its Suryavanshi rulers face severe perils as its primary river, the revered Saraswati, is slowly drying to extinction. They also face devastating terrorist attacks from the east, the land of the Chandravanshis. To make matters worse, the Chandravanshis appear to have allied with the Nagas, an ostracised and sinister race of deformed humans with astonishing martial skills!The only hope for the Suryavanshis is an ancient legend: When evil reaches epic proportions, when all seems lost, when it appears that your enemies have triumphed, a hero will emerge.Is the rough-hewn Tibetan immigrant Shiva, really that hero? And does he want to be that hero at all?       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4230687.Ashwin_Sanghi">About Ashwin Sanghi</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4230687.Ashwin_Sanghi"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1333093978p3/4230687.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4230687.Ashwin_Sanghi">Ashwin Sanghi
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,115
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5918133640091666125">Ashwin Sanghi—entrepreneur by day, novelist by night—has all the usual qualifications of an Indian businessman. Schooling at the Cathedral & John Connon School, a B.A. (Economics) from St. Xavier’s College, and an M.B.A. (Finance) from the Yale School of Management. Besides being a businessman, Ashwin manages a parallel career as writer of fiction. Ashwin’s first novel, ‘The Rozabal Line’ was orig</span>
  <span id="freeText5918133640091666125" style="display:none">Ashwin Sanghi—entrepreneur by day, novelist by night—has all the usual qualifications of an Indian businessman. Schooling at the Cathedral &amp; John Connon School, a B.A. (Economics) from St. Xavier’s College, and an M.B.A. (Finance) from the Yale School of Management. Besides being a businessman, Ashwin manages a parallel career as writer of fiction. Ashwin’s first novel, ‘The Rozabal Line’ was originally self-published in 2007 under his anagram-pseudonym—Shawn Haigins. The book was subsequently published by Westland in 2008 and 2010 in India under his own name and went on to become a national bestseller. ‘Chanakya’s Chant’ is his second novel in the historical-fiction genre. The book has remained on AC Nielsen’s India Bookscan Top-10 for all of 2011. It won the ‘2010 Crossword-Vodafone Popular Choice Award’ in September 2011. UTV has purchased the movie rights to the book and a film based upon the story is expected soon. Dr. Shashi Tharoor released the novel in Mumbai calling it an “enthralling, delightfully-interesting and gripping read with historical research that is impressive.” The Hindustan Times has called it “a cracker of a page-turner.” Ashwin is currently working on his third novel, as yet untitled, that explores business strategies in ancient India. Ashwin is also working towards a Ph.D. in Creative Writing from Bangor University in Wales. Ashwin lives in Mumbai with his wife, Anushika, and his eight-year old son, Raghuvir.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5918133640091666125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
